The Falasifa's Cosmology: Circular Motion as the Bridge
The falasifa's explanation of temporal events via eternal circular motion and souls.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the falasifa use eternal circular motion and celestial souls to explain the origination of temporal events from the eternal, addressing Ghazali's counter-argument.

Core Idea
Circular motion bridges the eternal and temporal by being perpetual yet composed of temporal parts.

After Ghazali's counter that the same problem applies to the intermediaries (preparation, time), the falasifa elaborate a detailed cosmological model. They argue that temporal events ultimately depend on the eternal circular motion of the heavens, which is caused by eternal souls. This motion, being both eternal in its continuity and temporal in its parts, serves as the necessary intermediate. Let's explore their response.

Guided Path
1
Read the falasifa's detailed explanation
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice how they build the causal chain: from eternal souls to circular motion to temporal events in the sublunary world.
2
Understand the role of circular motion
Why is circular motion special? It is eternal as a whole, but each part of it is temporal. This duality allows it to mediate between the eternal and temporal.
3
Grasp the role of celestial souls
The souls of the heavens are eternal and cause the circular motion. Since the soul is uniform, the motion is uniform and perpetual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاعتراض الثاني : على أصل دليلهم أن يقال : استبعدتم حدوث حادث من قديم ، ولابد لكم من الاعتراف به ، فإن فى العالم حوادث ولها أسباب ، فإن استندت الحوادث إلى الحوادث إلى غير نهاية ، فهو محال ، وليس ذلك معتقد عاقل ، ولو كان ذلك ممكناً لاستغنيتم عن الاعتراف بالصانع وإثبات واجب وجود هو مستند الممكنات ، و إذا كانت الحوادث لها طرف ينتهى إليه سلسلتها ، فيكون ذلك الطرف هو القديم ، فلابد إذن على أصلكم من تجويز صدور حادث من قديم . فإن قيل : نحن لا نبعد صدور حادث عن قديم أى حادث كان ، بل نبعد صدور حادث هو أول الحوادث من القديم ، إذ لا يفارق حال الحدوث ما قبله في ترجيح جهة الوجود ، لا من حيث حضور وقت ولا آلة ولا شرط ولا طبيعة ولا غرض ولا سبب من سبب من الأسباب ، فأما إذا لم يكن هو الحادث الأول. جاز يصدر منه عند حدوث شيء آخر من استعداد المحل القابل وحضور الوقت الموافق أو ما يجرى هذا المجرى . قلنا : فالسؤال فى حصول الاستعداد وحضور الوقت وكل ما يتجدد ، قائم . فإما أن يتسلسل إلى غير نهاية أو ينتهى إلى قديم يكون أول حادث منه . فإن قيل : المواد القابلة للصور والأعراض والكيفيات ليس شيء منها حادثاً . والكيفيات الحادثة هي حركة الأفلاك ، أعنى الحركة الدورية وما يتجدد من الأوصاف الإضافية لها ، من التثليث والتربيع والتسديس ، وهي نسبة بعض أجزاء الفلك والكواكب إلى بعض ، وبعضها نسبة إلى الأرض ، كما يحصل من الطلوع والشروق والزوال عن منتهى الارتفاع ، والبعد عن الأرض يكون الكوكب في الأوج ، والقرب بكونه فى الحضيض ، والميل عن بعض الأقطار بكونه في الشمال والجنوب ؛ وهذه الإضافة لازمة للحركة الدورية بالضرورة ، فموجبها الحركة الدورية ; وأما الحوادث فيما يحويه مقعر فلك القمر ، وهو العناصر الأربعة ، بما يعرض فيها من كون وفساد ، وامتزاج وافتراق ، واستحالة من صفة إلى صفة ، فكل ذلك حوادث مستند بعضها إلى بعض في تفصيل طويل ، و بالآخرة تنتهى مبادئ أسبابها إلى الحركة السماوية الدورية ، ونسب الكواكب بعضها إلى بعض أو نسبتها إلى الأرض فيخرج من مجموع ذلك أن الحركة الدورية الدائمة الأبدية ، مستند الحوادث كلها ، ومحرك السماء حركتها الدورية نفوس السموات ، فإنها حية نازلة منزلة نفوسنا بالنسبة إلى أبداننا ، ونفوسها قديمة ، فلا جرم أن الحركة الدورية التى هى موجبها أيضاً قديمة ، ولما تشابهت أحوال النفس لكونها قديمة ، تشابهت أحوال الحركات ، أي كانت دائرة أبداً فإذن لا يتصور أن يصدر الحادث من قديم إلا بواسطة حركة دورية ، تشبه القديم من وجه ، فإنه دائم أبداً ، وتشبه الحادث من وجه ، فإن أبدية كل جزء يفرض منها ، كان حادثاً بعد أن لم يكن ، فهو (١) من حيث إنه
The second objection: On the basis of their argument it is said: You have deemed improbable the occurrence of a temporal event from the eternal, yet you must acknowledge it, for in the world there are temporal events and they have causes. If the temporal events are traced back to temporal events ad infinitum, that is impossible, and no rational person holds that. And if that were possible, you would have dispensed with acknowledging the Maker and establishing the Necessary Existence who is the support of contingent things. And since temporal events have a limit at which their chain ends, that limit is the eternal. Therefore, according to your own principle, you must allow the occurrence of a temporal event from the eternal. If it is said: We do not deem improbable the occurrence of any temporal event from the eternal; rather, we deem improbable the occurrence of a temporal event that is the first of temporal events from the eternal, for the state of occurrence is not distinguished from what preceded it in preferring the side of existence, neither by the presence of a time, nor an instrument, nor a condition, nor a nature, nor a purpose, nor any cause of the causes. But if it is not the first temporal event, it is possible for it to occur from it when another thing occurs, such as the preparation of the receptive substrate and the coming of the suitable time, or what is of this kind. We say: The question about the occurrence of the preparation and the coming of the time and everything that is renewed remains. Either it leads to an infinite regress or it ends with an eternal that is the first temporal event from it. If it is said: The materials receptive of forms, accidents, and qualities are not temporal at all. The temporal qualities are the motion of the spheres, that is, circular motion, and what is renewed of its additional attributes, such as trine, square, and sextile aspects, which are the ratios of some parts of the celestial sphere and planets to others, and some of their ratios to the earth, as occurs from rising, setting, culmination, and distance from the earth when the planet is in apogee, or proximity when it is in perigee, and inclination from some regions when it is in the north or south. Thus from all this it emerges that the perpetual eternal circular motion is the support of all temporal events. The mover of the heaven in its circular motion is the souls of the heavens, for they are living, analogous to our souls in relation to our bodies, and their souls are eternal. Hence the circular motion which is their effect is also eternal. And since the states of the soul are uniform because it is eternal, the states of the motions are uniform, meaning they are perpetually circular. Therefore, it is inconceivable that a temporal event should proceed from the eternal except by means of a circular motion which resembles the eternal in one respect, for it is perpetually eternal, and resembles the temporal in another respect, for the eternity of each part that is supposed from it is temporal after having been non-existent. So it (the motion) is, in that it...

Commentary
This passage is the second objection and its response. Ghazali begins by pointing out that the falasifa must admit the occurrence of a temporal event from an eternal being, because temporal events exist, their chain of causes cannot go back infinitely, and must end with an eternal cause. The falasifa respond that they only deny the first temporal event; later events can occur through intermediates like the preparation of matter and suitable time. Ghazali retorts that the same question applies to these intermediates, leading to an infinite regress or a first temporal event. The falasifa then elaborate their cosmology: the ultimate temporal events depend on the eternal circular motion of the heavens, which is caused by eternal souls. The circular motion is both eternal (as a whole) and temporal (in its parts), and thus serves as a bridge. Ghazali's objection is that this does not truly solve the problem, as the origin of the motion itself remains unexplained.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The falasifa argue that the eternal cannot directly produce temporal events without a bridge. Do you live as though you need intermediaries—such as your own skills, status, or routines—to receive what only God can give directly? What would it mean for your daily reliance on Him if you truly believed He can create from nothing without any means?
?
The souls of the heavens are described as eternal and uniform, producing a motion that never changes. In contrast, your own soul is created and constantly changing. When you reflect on your desires, decisions, and spiritual states, do you act as if your soul is self-sufficient and independent, or do you recognize that every moment of existence and stability is a gift from God? How would this recognition change the way you pray, work, and relate to others today?
?
Each part of circular motion is temporal—it comes and goes. Consider your own actions: they are temporal events that appear and vanish. Do you truly believe that each action is created directly by God at every instant, or do you implicitly rely on your own power and continuity? What would it look like to live with constant awareness that 'there is no power nor strength except with God' (lā ḥawla wa lā quwwata illā billāh) in every single deed you do?

The Philosophers' Theory of Circular Motion as Mediator
Philosophers argue that circular motion mediates between eternal and temporal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' claim that perpetual circular motion is the necessary intermediary between the eternal and the temporal.

Core Idea
Perpetual motion is the philosophers' bridge between the eternal and the temporal.

In this passage, Ghazali presents the detailed argument of the philosophers who claim that temporal events can only proceed from the eternal through a perpetual circular motion. They attempt to show that the circular motion of the heavens, being both eternal in its continuity and temporal in its parts, serves as the necessary link. This lesson unpacks their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the philosophers' exposition
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully to understand the full theory.
Notice the structure: initial problem, then their response.
2
Identify the key components
Notice how they distinguish between the eternal souls of the heavens, the perpetual motion, and the temporal events in the sublunary world.
3
Consider the role of relations
The philosophers rely on relational descriptions (trine, square, etc.) to explain how the motion produces temporal effects.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The philosophers conclude that circular motion is both eternal and temporal, thus mediating between the two.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جاز يصدر منه عند حدوث شيء آخر من استعداد المحل القابل وحضور الوقت الموافق أو ما يجرى هذا المجرى . قلنا : فالسؤال فى حصول الاستعداد وحضور الوقت وكل ما يتجدد ، قائم . فإما أن يتسلسل إلى غير نهاية أو ينتهى إلى قديم يكون أول حادث منه . فإن قيل : المواد القابلة للصور والأعراض والكيفيات ليس شيء منها حادثاً . والكيفيات الحادثة هي حركة الأفلاك ، أعنى الحركة الدورية وما يتجدد من الأوصاف الإضافية لها ، من التثليث والتربيع والتسديس ، وهي نسبة بعض أجزاء الفلك والكواكب إلى بعض ، وبعضها نسبة إلى الأرض ، كما يحصل من الطلوع والشروق والزوال عن منتهى الارتفاع ، والبعد عن الأرض يكون الكوكب في الأوج ، والقرب بكونه فى الحضيض ، والميل عن بعض الأقطار بكونه في الشمال والجنوب ؛ وهذه الإضافة لازمة للحركة الدورية بالضرورة ، فموجبها الحركة الدورية ؛ وأما الحوادث فيما يحويه مقعر فلك القمر ، وهو العناصر الأربعة ، بما يعرض فيها من كون وفساد ، وامتزاج وافتراق ، واستحالة من صفة إلى صفة ، فكل ذلك حوادث مستند بعضها إلى بعض في تفصيل طويل ، و بالآخرة تنتهى مبادئ أسبابها إلى الحركة السماوية الدورية ، ونسب الكواكب بعضها إلى بعض أو نسبتها إلى الأرض فيخرج من مجموع ذلك أن الحركة الدورية الدائمة الأبدية ، مستند الحوادث كلها ، ومحرك السماء حركتها الدورية نفوس السموات ، فإنها حية نازلة منزلة نفوسنا بالنسبة إلى أبداننا ، ونفوسها قديمة ، فلا جرم أن الحركة الدورية التى هى موجبها أيضاً قديمة ، ولما تشابهت أحوال النفس لكونها قديمة ، تشابهت أحوال الحركات ، أي كانت دائرة أبداً فإذن لا يتصور أن يصدر الحادث من قديم إلا بواسطة حركة دورية ، تشبه القديم من وجه ، فإنه دائم أبداً ، وتشبه الحادث من وجه ، فإن أبدية كل جزء يفرض منها ، كان حادثاً بعد أن لم يكن ، فهي من حيث إنها حادث بأجزائه وإضافاته ، مبدأ الحوادث ومن حيث إنها أبدى متشابه الأحوال ، صادر عن نفس أزلية ؛ فإن كان في العالم حوادث فلا بد من حركة دورية ، وفى العالم حوادث ؛ فالحركة الدورية الأبدية ، ثابتة . المستند حادثة قلنا : هذا التطويل لا يغنيكم ، فإن الحركة الدورية التي هي أم قديمة ؟! فإن كانت قديمة فكيف صارت مبدأ لأول الحوادث ؟! وإن كانت حادثة افتقرت إلى حادث آخر ، وتسلسل الأمر ، وقولكم : إنه من وجه يشبه القديم ، ومن وجه يشبه الحادث، فإنه ثابت متجدد ، أي هو ثابت التجدد ، متجدد الثبوت فنقول : أهو مبدأ الحوادث من حيث إنه ثابت ، أو من حيث إنه متجدد ؟ ! فإن كان من حيث إنه ثابت ، فكيف صدر من ثابت متشابه الأحوال شيء في بعض الأوقات دون بعض ؟ ! وإن كان من حيث إنه متجدد ، فها سبب تجدده في نفسه ؟ ! فيحتاج إلى سبب آخر ويتسلسل فهذا غاية تقرير الإلزام ولهم في الخروج عن هذا الإلزام نوع احتيال سنورده في بعض المسائل بعد هذه ، كيلا يطول كلام هذه المسألة بانشعاب شجون الكلام وفنونه ، على أنا سنبين أن الحركة الدورية لا تصلح أن تكون مبدأ الحوادث ، فإن جميع الحوادث مخترعة لله ابتداء ، ونبطل ما قالوه : من كون السماء حيواناً متحركاً بالاختيار ، حركة نفسية كحركتنا
It may originate from Him when another thing occurs, such as the preparedness of the receptive substrate, the presence of the suitable time, or whatever runs in this course. We say: The question about the occurrence of preparedness, the presence of time, and everything that becomes new, remains. Either it goes on ad infinitum or it ends with an eternal being which is the first temporal thing from it. If it is said: The materials receptive of forms, accidents, and qualities are none of them temporal. The temporal qualities are the motion of the spheres, that is, the circular motion and what becomes new of their relational descriptions, such as trine, square, and sextile—these are the relation of some parts of the sphere and planets to others, and some of them relation to the earth, as occurs from rising, dawning, and departure from the maximum height, and distance from the earth causes the planet to be at apogee, and proximity causes it to be at perigee, and inclination from some regions causes it to be in the north or south; and this relation is necessarily concomitant with circular motion, so its cause is circular motion. As for the temporal events in what is contained by the concave of the sphere of the moon—that is, the four elements—including what occurs in them of generation and corruption, mixture and separation, and transformation from one attribute to another—all that is temporal events, some depending on others in a long detail, and ultimately the principles of their causes end at the celestial circular motion and the relations of the planets to each other or their relation to the earth. From all that it follows that the perpetual eternal circular motion is the basis of all temporal events. The mover of the heaven in its circular motion is the souls of the heavens, for they are living beings in the status of our souls relative to our bodies, and their souls are eternal; inevitably the circular motion which is their effect is also eternal. And since the states of the soul are similar because it is eternal, the states of the motions are similar, i.e., they were always circular eternally. Therefore, it is inconceivable that a temporal event should proceed from the eternal except through a circular motion which resembles the eternal in one respect—for it is perpetual eternally—and resembles the temporal in another respect—for the perpetuity of each part that one supposes of it is temporal, having come to be after it was not. So it is, insofar as it is temporal in its parts and relations, the principle of temporal events; and insofar as it is eternal and uniform in states, it proceeds from an eternal soul. If there are temporal events in the world, there must be a circular motion; and there are temporal events in the world; thus the eternal circular motion is established. Its basis is temporal? We say: This lengthy discourse does not avail you. For the circular motion—is it eternal or temporal?! If it is eternal, how did it become the principle of the first temporal event?! If it is temporal, it would require another temporal event, leading to infinite regress. And your statement that it resembles the eternal in one respect and the temporal in another—it is constant and renewing, i.e., it is constant in renewal, renewing in constancy. We say: Is it the principle of temporal events insofar as it is constant, or insofar as it is renewing?! If insofar as it is constant, how did something issue from a constant uniform state at some times and not others?! If insofar as it is renewing, then what is the cause of its renewal in itself?! It would need another cause, leading to infinite regress. This is the fullest presentation of the constraint. And they have a kind of subterfuge to escape this constraint, which we will present in some later questions, so that the discussion of this question does not become prolonged by the branching of its themes and varieties. Moreover, we will show that circular motion is not fit to be the principle of temporal events, for all temporal events are created by God from the beginning, and we will invalidate their claim that the heaven is an animal moving by choice, with a psychic motion like our motion.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage presents a sustained argument and refutation. It begins with an implicit objection: it might be said that the eternal can give rise to a temporal event only when another temporal condition occurs (like preparedness or suitable time). Ghazali immediately counters: that condition itself is temporal, leading either to infinite regress or an eternal first temporal event. He then, in the voice of the philosophers, offers a detailed theory: the materials of the sublunary world are not themselves temporal; temporal qualities arise from the circular motion of the heavens and their relational descriptions (trine, square, etc.), which are necessary concomitants of that motion. All sublunary generation and corruption ultimately trace back to this perpetual circular motion. The motion is caused by the eternal souls of the heavens, which are like our souls but eternal. Because the soul is eternal, its effect (circular motion) is also eternal and uniform, yet each part of that motion is temporal, providing a link between the eternal and the temporal. Thus, the philosophers conclude, temporal events can only proceed from the eternal through such a motion. Ghazali then refutes this: if the circular motion is eternal, it cannot be the cause of the first temporal event, since an eternal cause would produce its effect eternally, not at a particular time. If it is temporal, it requires another cause, leading to infinite regress. The philosophers' claim that it is 'constant and renewing' fails because if it is constant, it cannot explain why a temporal event occurs at one time rather than another; if it is renewing, that renewal itself needs a cause. Ghazali concludes that this is a decisive refutation, though he postpones his own full demonstration that all temporal events are directly created by God and that the heaven is not a self-moving animal.

Key Terms
حركة دورية (circular motion)
نفوس السموات (souls of the heavens)
قديم (eternal)
حادث (temporal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers, what makes the circular motion a suitable intermediary between the eternal and the temporal?
A) It is entirely eternal.
B) It is entirely temporal.
C) It is both eternal in its continuity and temporal in its parts.
D) It is caused by a temporal soul.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers argue that perpetual circular motion, being both eternal and temporal, is the only way temporal events can proceed from an eternal source.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The philosophers placed their trust in an eternal motion and souls to explain how things happen. In your daily life, do you ever rely on 'natural laws' or 'causes' as if they were independent of Allah? How does this lesson challenge you to see all events as directly from Allah?
?
When you observe the regular cycles of day and night, seasons, or your own routines, do you attribute them to innate properties of creation, or do you remember that Allah sustains them each moment? What would change if you consciously affirmed Allah's direct control over every detail?
?
The philosophers argued that the eternal cannot directly produce the temporal without a mediator. Do you ever feel that Allah is 'distant' or that your prayers need intermediaries to reach Him? How does Ghazali's rebuttal (implied in this passage) call you to immediate reliance on Allah alone?

Ghazali's Refutation: The Dilemma of Eternal or Temporal Motion
Ghazali refutes the philosophers' theory with a dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's refutation of the philosophers' claim by showing the inherent contradiction in the notion of an intermediary that is both constant and renewing.

Core Idea
If circular motion is eternal, it cannot cause a first temporal event; if temporal, it requires another cause.

Having presented the philosophers' theory, Ghazali now delivers his refutation. He exposes a central dilemma: the circular motion cannot be both the principle of temporal events and the effect of an eternal cause without leading to absurdities. This lesson examines his incisive critique.

Guided Path
1
Read Ghazali's objection
Read the Arabic passage focusing on the dilemma.
Pay attention to the two-part question: 'is it eternal or temporal?'
2
Analyze the two options
Ghazali asks: is the motion eternal or temporal? Each leads to a problem.
3
Examine the 'constant and renewing' claim
Ghazali challenges the philosophers' characterization by asking what aspect makes it the principle.
4
Understand the conclusion
Ghazali defers further discussion but asserts that circular motion is unfit and that all events are directly from God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جاز يصدر منه عند حدوث شيء آخر من استعداد المحل القابل وحضور الوقت الموافق أو ما يجرى هذا المجرى . قلنا : فالسؤال فى حصول الاستعداد وحضور الوقت وكل ما يتجدد ، قائم . فإما أن يتسلسل إلى غير نهاية أو ينتهى إلى قديم يكون أول حادث منه . فإن قيل : المواد القابلة للصور والأعراض والكيفيات ليس شيء منها حادثاً . والكيفيات الحادثة هي حركة الأفلاك ، أعنى الحركة الدورية وما يتجدد من الأوصاف الإضافية لها ، من التثليث والتربيع والتسديس ، وهي نسبة بعض أجزاء الفلك والكواكب إلى بعض ، وبعضها نسبة إلى الأرض ، كما يحصل من الطلوع والشروق والزوال عن منتهى الارتفاع ، والبعد عن الأرض يكون الكوكب في الأوج ، والقرب بكونه فى الحضيض ، والميل عن بعض الأقطار بكونه في الشمال والجنوب ؛ وهذه الإضافة لازمة للحركة الدورية بالضرورة ، فموجبها الحركة الدورية ؛ وأما الحوادث فيما يحويه مقعر فلك القمر ، وهو العناصر الأربعة ، بما يعرض فيها من كون وفساد ، وامتزاج وافتراق ، واستحالة من صفة إلى صفة ، فكل ذلك حوادث مستند بعضها إلى بعض في تفصيل طويل ، و بالآخرة تنتهى مبادئ أسبابها إلى الحركة السماوية الدورية ، ونسب الكواكب بعضها إلى بعض أو نسبتها إلى الأرض فيخرج من مجموع ذلك أن الحركة الدورية الدائمة الأبدية ، مستند الحوادث كلها ، ومحرك السماء حركتها الدورية نفوس السموات ، فإنها حية نازلة منزلة نفوسنا بالنسبة إلى أبداننا ، ونفوسها قديمة ، فلا جرم أن الحركة الدورية التى هى موجبها أيضاً قديمة ، ولما تشابهت أحوال النفس لكونها قديمة ، تشابهت أحوال الحركات ، أي كانت دائرة أبداً فإذن لا يتصور أن يصدر الحادث من قديم إلا بواسطة حركة دورية ، تشبه القديم من وجه ، فإنه دائم أبداً ، وتشبه الحادث من وجه ، فإن أبدية كل جزء يفرض منها ، كان حادثاً بعد أن لم يكن ، فهي من حيث إنها حادث بأجزائه وإضافاته ، مبدأ الحوادث ومن حيث إنها أبدى متشابه الأحوال ، صادر عن نفس أزلية ؛ فإن كان في العالم حوادث فلا بد من حركة دورية ، وفى العالم حوادث ؛ فالحركة الدورية الأبدية ، ثابتة . المستند حادثة قلنا : هذا التطويل لا يغنيكم ، فإن الحركة الدورية التي هي أم قديمة ؟! فإن كانت قديمة فكيف صارت مبدأ لأول الحوادث ؟! وإن كانت حادثة افتقرت إلى حادث آخر ، وتسلسل الأمر ، وقولكم : إنه من وجه يشبه القديم ، ومن وجه يشبه الحادث، فإنه ثابت متجدد ، أي هو ثابت التجدد ، متجدد الثبوت فنقول : أهو مبدأ الحوادث من حيث إنه ثابت ، أو من حيث إنه متجدد ؟ ! فإن كان من حيث إنه ثابت ، فكيف صدر من ثابت متشابه الأحوال شيء في بعض الأوقات دون بعض ؟ ! وإن كان من حيث إنه متجدد ، فها سبب تجدده في نفسه ؟ ! فيحتاج إلى سبب آخر ويتسلسل فهذا غاية تقرير الإلزام ولهم في الخروج عن هذا الإلزام نوع احتيال سنورده في بعض المسائل بعد هذه ، كيلا يطول كلام هذه المسألة بانشعاب شجون الكلام وفنونه ، على أنا سنبين أن الحركة الدورية لا تصلح أن تكون مبدأ الحوادث ، فإن جميع الحوادث مخترعة لله ابتداء ، ونبطل ما قالوه : من كون السماء حيواناً متحركاً بالاختيار ، حركة نفسية كحركتنا
It may originate from Him when another thing occurs, such as the preparedness of the receptive substrate, the presence of the suitable time, or whatever runs in this course. We say: The question about the occurrence of preparedness, the presence of time, and everything that becomes new, remains. Either it goes on ad infinitum or it ends with an eternal being which is the first temporal thing from it. If it is said: The materials receptive of forms, accidents, and qualities are none of them temporal. The temporal qualities are the motion of the spheres, that is, the circular motion and what becomes new of their relational descriptions, such as trine, square, and sextile—these are the relation of some parts of the sphere and planets to others, and some of them relation to the earth, as occurs from rising, dawning, and departure from the maximum height, and distance from the earth causes the planet to be at apogee, and proximity causes it to be at perigee, and inclination from some regions causes it to be in the north or south; and this relation is necessarily concomitant with circular motion, so its cause is circular motion. As for the temporal events in what is contained by the concave of the sphere of the moon—that is, the four elements—including what occurs in them of generation and corruption, mixture and separation, and transformation from one attribute to another—all that is temporal events, some depending on others in a long detail, and ultimately the principles of their causes end at the celestial circular motion and the relations of the planets to each other or their relation to the earth. From all that it follows that the perpetual eternal circular motion is the basis of all temporal events. The mover of the heaven in its circular motion is the souls of the heavens, for they are living beings in the status of our souls relative to our bodies, and their souls are eternal; inevitably the circular motion which is their effect is also eternal. And since the states of the soul are similar because it is eternal, the states of the motions are similar, i.e., they were always circular eternally. Therefore, it is inconceivable that a temporal event should proceed from the eternal except through a circular motion which resembles the eternal in one respect—for it is perpetual eternally—and resembles the temporal in another respect—for the perpetuity of each part that one supposes of it is temporal, having come to be after it was not. So it is, insofar as it is temporal in its parts and relations, the principle of temporal events; and insofar as it is eternal and uniform in states, it proceeds from an eternal soul. If there are temporal events in the world, there must be a circular motion; and there are temporal events in the world; thus the eternal circular motion is established. Its basis is temporal? We say: This lengthy discourse does not avail you. For the circular motion—is it eternal or temporal?! If it is eternal, how did it become the principle of the first temporal event?! If it is temporal, it would require another temporal event, leading to infinite regress. And your statement that it resembles the eternal in one respect and the temporal in another—it is constant and renewing, i.e., it is constant in renewal, renewing in constancy. We say: Is it the principle of temporal events insofar as it is constant, or insofar as it is renewing?! If insofar as it is constant, how did something issue from a constant uniform state at some times and not others?! If insofar as it is renewing, then what is the cause of its renewal in itself?! It would need another cause, leading to infinite regress. This is the fullest presentation of the constraint. And they have a kind of subterfuge to escape this constraint, which we will present in some later questions, so that the discussion of this question does not become prolonged by the branching of its themes and varieties. Moreover, we will show that circular motion is not fit to be the principle of temporal events, for all temporal events are created by God from the beginning, and we will invalidate their claim that the heaven is an animal moving by choice, with a psychic motion like our motion.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage presents a sustained argument and refutation. It begins with an implicit objection: it might be said that the eternal can give rise to a temporal event only when another temporal condition occurs (like preparedness or suitable time). Ghazali immediately counters: that condition itself is temporal, leading either to infinite regress or an eternal first temporal event. He then, in the voice of the philosophers, offers a detailed theory: the materials of the sublunary world are not themselves temporal; temporal qualities arise from the circular motion of the heavens and their relational descriptions (trine, square, etc.), which are necessary concomitants of that motion. All sublunary generation and corruption ultimately trace back to this perpetual circular motion. The motion is caused by the eternal souls of the heavens, which are like our souls but eternal. Because the soul is eternal, its effect (circular motion) is also eternal and uniform, yet each part of that motion is temporal, providing a link between the eternal and the temporal. Thus, the philosophers conclude, temporal events can only proceed from the eternal through such a motion. Ghazali then refutes this: if the circular motion is eternal, it cannot be the cause of the first temporal event, since an eternal cause would produce its effect eternally, not at a particular time. If it is temporal, it requires another cause, leading to infinite regress. The philosophers' claim that it is 'constant and renewing' fails because if it is constant, it cannot explain why a temporal event occurs at one time rather than another; if it is renewing, that renewal itself needs a cause. Ghazali concludes that this is a decisive refutation, though he postpones his own full demonstration that all temporal events are directly created by God and that the heaven is not a self-moving animal.

Key Terms
قديم (eternal)
حادث (temporal)
تسلسل (infinite regress)
ثابت (constant)
متجدد (renewing)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The philosophers' claim that perpetual circular motion is a valid intermediary between the eternal and the temporal is a genuine solution.
Correction: Ghazali shows it leads to a contradiction: if it is eternal, it cannot cause temporal events; if temporal, it requires another cause.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what problem arises if the circular motion is said to be eternal?
A) It would be too simple.
B) It cannot be the principle of the first temporal event because an eternal cause would produce effects uniformly.
C) It would conflict with the soul's eternity.
D) It would require a cause.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali's refutation hinges on the impossibility of an eternal cause producing a first temporal event without introducing an infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you often attribute the events in your life to 'natural causes' or 'coincidence' without recognizing that every single moment is directly sustained by Allah? How would your attitude change if you truly believed that no 'eternal motion' could ever produce a single event without His will?
?
The philosophers claimed that the heavens move by their own nature. In your own life, have you ever felt self-sufficient, as if your actions or habits could sustain themselves without needing Allah's constant renewal? What would it mean for you to acknowledge that even your most consistent traits are created anew by Allah every moment?
?
Ghazali's argument against infinite regress forces you to confront the fact that every chain must have a first cause. Where in your life have you been avoiding tracing things back to Allah—perhaps by assuming that your own efforts or the systems around you are ultimate causes? What step will you take today to make that connection explicit in your heart?

The Two Meanings of Priority
Ghazali presents the philosophers' distinction between essential and temporal priority with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between essential priority (al-taqaddum bi al-dhat) and temporal priority (al-taqaddum bi al-zaman), and why essential priority does not entail temporal separation.

Core Idea
Priority can be essential without being temporal.

Ghazali begins the second proof by clarifying what 'priority' means when saying the world is posterior to God. The philosophers argue that priority can be either essential or temporal. Essential priority, like the priority of a cause over its effect, can coexist in time. This lesson explores that distinction and its first consequence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage identifying the two types of priority
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the phrases 'bi al-dhat' and 'bi al-zaman'. Notice the examples given.
The passage uses the word 'إما' to present alternatives.
2
Understand the examples of essential priority
The example of one over two shows natural priority without time difference. The cause-effect examples (hand and shadow, hand and ring, hand and water) show that cause is prior in essence while both are simultaneous.
These illustrate that essential priority does not require temporal precedence.
3
Consider the first scenario: essential priority of God
If God's priority is essential, then God and the world share the same temporal status—both must be originated or both eternal, because essential priority does not involve time.
This shows that essential priority alone cannot explain the world's temporal origination.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that if priority is essential, it is impossible for one to be eternal and the other originated. This sets up the alternative temporal priority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليل ثان لهم في المسألة زعموا أن القائل : بأن العالم متأخر عن الله ، والله متقدم عليه ، ليس يخلو إما أن يريد به أنه متقدم بالذات لا بالزمان ، كتقدم الواحد على الاثنين ، فإنه بالطبع ، مع أنه يجوز أن يكون معه في الوجود الزماني ، وكتقدم العلة على المعلول ، مثل تقدم حركة الشخص ، على حركة الظل التابع له ، وكحركة اليد حركة الخاتم ، وحركة اليد في الماء مع حركة الماء ، فإنها متساوية في الزمان وبعضها علة وبعضها معلول ، إذ يقال : تحرك الظل لحركة الشخص ، وتحرك الماء لحركة اليد في الماء ، ولا يقال تحرك الشخص لحركة الظل ، ولا تحركت اليد لحركة الماء ، وإن كانت متساوية فإن أريد بتقدم البارى على العالم هذا ، لزم أن يكونا حادثين أو قديمين ، واستحال أن يكون أحدهما قديماً والآخر حادثاً ؛ وإن أريد به أن البارى متقدم على العالم والزمان لا بالذات بل بالزمان ؛ فإذن قبل وجود العالم والزمان زمان كان العالم فيه معدوماً ، إذ كان العدم سابقاً على الوجود ، وكان الله سابقاً بمدة مديدة لها طرف من جهة الآخر ، ولا طرف لها من جهة الأول ؛ فإذن قبل الزمان زمان لا نهاية له وهو متناقض ، ولأجله يستحيل القول بحدوث الزمان ، وإذا وجب قدم الزمان ، وهو عبارة عن قدر الحركة ، وجب قدم الحركة ، ووجب قدم المتحرك الذي يدوم الزمان بدوام حركته .
A second proof for them regarding the issue. They claimed that the one who says that the world is posterior to God, and God is prior to it, must either mean: that He is prior in essence, not in time—like the priority of the one over two, for it is by nature, while it is possible for it to coexist with it in temporal existence; and like the priority of the cause over the effect, such as the priority of the movement of the person over the movement of the shadow that follows him, and like the movement of the hand [over] the movement of the ring, and the movement of the hand in the water together with the movement of the water, for they are simultaneous in time, some of them being cause and some effect, since it is said: the shadow moves due to the movement of the person, and the water moves due to the movement of the hand in the water, and it is not said: the person moves due to the movement of the shadow, nor the hand moves due to the movement of the water, even though they are simultaneous. If by this is meant the priority of the Creator over the world, then it would necessitate that both be originated or both be eternal, and it would be impossible for one to be eternal and the other originated. And if by it is meant that the Creator is prior to the world and time not in essence but in time, then before the existence of the world and time there was a time in which the world was non-existent, since non-existence preceded existence, and God was prior by an extended period that has an end from the one direction and no end from the first direction. So before time there is time without end, which is contradictory, and for that reason it is impossible to say that time is originated. And if the eternity of time is necessary—and it is an expression of the measure of motion—then the eternity of motion is necessary, and the eternity of the mover whose duration continues due to the duration of its motion is necessary.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage presents the philosophers' second proof for the eternity of the world, specifically focusing on the concept of priority. Ghazali first explains the two possible meanings of 'priority' (taqaddum): priority in essence (bi al-dhat) and priority in time (bi al-zaman). He gives examples: the priority of the one over two is by nature, yet they can coexist in time; the priority of a cause over its effect can be simultaneous (like hand and shadow movement). If God's priority over the world is understood as essential priority, then both God and the world must share the same temporal status—both originated or both eternal—because essential priority does not entail temporal precedence. If God's priority is temporal, then before the world and time there must have been a time when the world was non-existent, implying a time before time, which leads to an infinite regress. Thus, time cannot be originated; it must be eternal, and consequently motion and the moving body (the celestial sphere) must also be eternal. The proof aims to show that the only consistent view is the eternity of time and motion.

Key Terms
تقدم بالذات
تقدم بالزمان
علة
معلول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Priority always implies temporal precedence.
Correction: Essential priority does not involve time; a cause can be prior in essence while existing simultaneously with its effect.

Checkpoint
Which of the following best illustrates essential priority?
A) A father is prior to his son in time.
B) The movement of a hand is prior in essence to the movement of a shadow it casts, even if they are simultaneous.
C) The number two is prior to the number one in time.
D) God is prior to the world in time.

Key Takeaway
Essential priority does not require time difference; God's priority over the world, if essential, would not allow one to be eternal and the other originated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear that 'God is prior to the world', does your mind automatically picture a timeline? This lesson forces you to ask: is my mental picture of God's priority rooted in scripture or in my own temporal assumptions? Are you willing to uproot that image and replace it with a deeper causal understanding?
?
The philosophers argue that if God's priority is essential (causal), then the world cannot be originated—it must be co-eternal. This directly challenges Islamic belief. Have you ever felt the weight of this argument? If a friend asked you this today, could you respond using Ghazali's distinction, or would you stumble? Commit now to memorizing the two types of priority and their examples.
?
The example of the hand moving the ring: they are simultaneous, yet one is cause and one is effect. Do you live as if your actions are the cause of your outcomes, forgetting that God is the true cause? This lesson calls you to reorient your dependence. Will you consciously affirm today that every effect in your life is ultimately from God, even if it appears simultaneous with worldly causes?

The Infinite Regress Argument for Time's Eternity
Ghazali presents the philosophers' regress argument for the eternity of time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophical argument that if God's priority is temporal, it leads to an infinite regress, thus time must be eternal.

Core Idea
Temporal priority of God leads to time before time, a contradiction.

The philosophers now consider the second option: if God's priority is temporal, then before the world and time there must have been a time when the world did not exist, implying an infinite temporal regress. This contradiction forces the conclusion that time cannot have a beginning, so time, motion, and the moving body must be eternal. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on temporal priority
Read the Arabic and translation from 'وإن أريد به أن البارى متقدم على العالم والزمان لا بالذات بل بالزمان' to the end.
Notice the conditional structure: 'if... then'.
2
Identify the consequence of temporal priority
If God is temporally prior, then before the world existed there was a time when the world was non-existent. This implies a time before time.
The phrase 'قبل وجود العالم والزمان زمان' is key.
3
Understand the contradiction
The passage states that there would be a time with no beginning (no end from the first direction), which is contradictory because time is defined by before and after.
The phrase 'لا نهاية له' indicates an infinite regress.
4
See the conclusion
Because the assumption leads to a contradiction, the philosophers assert that time cannot be originated; it must be eternal. Consequently, motion and the moving body (the celestial sphere) are also eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليل ثان لهم في المسألة زعموا أن القائل : بأن العالم متأخر عن الله ، والله متقدم عليه ، ليس يخلو إما أن يريد به أنه متقدم بالذات لا بالزمان ، كتقدم الواحد على الاثنين ، فإنه بالطبع ، مع أنه يجوز أن يكون معه في الوجود الزماني ، وكتقدم العلة على المعلول ، مثل تقدم حركة الشخص ، على حركة الظل التابع له ، وكحركة اليد حركة الخاتم ، وحركة اليد في الماء مع حركة الماء ، فإنها متساوية في الزمان وبعضها علة وبعضها معلول ، إذ يقال : تحرك الظل لحركة الشخص ، وتحرك الماء لحركة اليد في الماء ، ولا يقال تحرك الشخص لحركة الظل ، ولا تحركت اليد لحركة الماء ، وإن كانت متساوية فإن أريد بتقدم البارى على العالم هذا ، لزم أن يكونا حادثين أو قديمين ، واستحال أن يكون أحدهما قديماً والآخر حادثاً ؛ وإن أريد به أن البارى متقدم على العالم والزمان لا بالذات بل بالزمان ؛ فإذن قبل وجود العالم والزمان زمان كان العالم فيه معدوماً ، إذ كان العدم سابقاً على الوجود ، وكان الله سابقاً بمدة مديدة لها طرف من جهة الآخر ، ولا طرف لها من جهة الأول ؛ فإذن قبل الزمان زمان لا نهاية له وهو متناقض ، ولأجله يستحيل القول بحدوث الزمان ، وإذا وجب قدم الزمان ، وهو عبارة عن قدر الحركة ، وجب قدم الحركة ، ووجب قدم المتحرك الذي يدوم الزمان بدوام حركته .
A second proof for them regarding the issue. They claimed that the one who says that the world is posterior to God, and God is prior to it, must either mean: that He is prior in essence, not in time—like the priority of the one over two, for it is by nature, while it is possible for it to coexist with it in temporal existence; and like the priority of the cause over the effect, such as the priority of the movement of the person over the movement of the shadow that follows him, and like the movement of the hand [over] the movement of the ring, and the movement of the hand in the water together with the movement of the water, for they are simultaneous in time, some of them being cause and some effect, since it is said: the shadow moves due to the movement of the person, and the water moves due to the movement of the hand in the water, and it is not said: the person moves due to the movement of the shadow, nor the hand moves due to the movement of the water, even though they are simultaneous. If by this is meant the priority of the Creator over the world, then it would necessitate that both be originated or both be eternal, and it would be impossible for one to be eternal and the other originated. And if by it is meant that the Creator is prior to the world and time not in essence but in time, then before the existence of the world and time there was a time in which the world was non-existent, since non-existence preceded existence, and God was prior by an extended period that has an end from the one direction and no end from the first direction. So before time there is time without end, which is contradictory, and for that reason it is impossible to say that time is originated. And if the eternity of time is necessary—and it is an expression of the measure of motion—then the eternity of motion is necessary, and the eternity of the mover whose duration continues due to the duration of its motion is necessary.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage presents the philosophers' second proof for the eternity of the world, specifically focusing on the concept of priority. Ghazali first explains the two possible meanings of 'priority' (taqaddum): priority in essence (bi al-dhat) and priority in time (bi al-zaman). He gives examples: the priority of the one over two is by nature, yet they can coexist in time; the priority of a cause over its effect can be simultaneous (like hand and shadow movement). If God's priority over the world is understood as essential priority, then both God and the world must share the same temporal status—both originated or both eternal—because essential priority does not entail temporal precedence. If God's priority is temporal, then before the world and time there must have been a time when the world was non-existent, implying a time before time, which leads to an infinite regress. Thus, time cannot be originated; it must be eternal, and consequently motion and the moving body (the celestial sphere) must also be eternal. The proof aims to show that the only consistent view is the eternity of time and motion.

Key Terms
حدوث الزمان
قدم الزمان
الحركة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God is prior in time, then time can have a beginning.
Correction: The argument shows that temporal priority of God implies a time before time, which is an infinite regress and contradictory, so time cannot have a beginning.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers' argument, what follows from assuming God's priority is temporal?
A) Time must have a beginning.
B) Time must be eternal.
C) The world is eternal but time is originated.
D) There is no need to assume time exists.

Key Takeaway
Time cannot be originated because that would require a time before time, which is absurd; hence time, motion, and the mover are eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'God existed before creation,' do you subconsciously imagine a timeline stretching back infinitely? How does the infinite regress argument expose the absurdity of that mental image?
?
The philosophers concluded that time and motion must be eternal to avoid a contradiction. Does your heart feel uncomfortable with the idea of anything existing co-eternally with God? What does that reveal about your understanding of God's absolute uniqueness?
?
If God's priority is not temporal but essential, then He is not bounded by time. How does that change the urgency with which you turn to Him in prayer? Are you living as if you have endless time, or as if every moment is directly before the Eternal?

Ghazali's First Objection: Time is Created
Ghazali refutes the philosophers by asserting time is created and redefining priority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's argument that time is created and that God's priority is existential, not temporal.

Core Idea
Time is created; God's priority is not temporal but existential.

In this passage, Imam Ghazali directly challenges the philosophers' proof that the world is eternal by asserting that time itself is created. He redefines what it means for God to be 'prior' to the world, stripping away the notion of a temporal interval and showing that priority is merely existential. This objection attacks the very foundation of the philosophers' argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand Ghazali's main claim
Read the opening sentence where Ghazali asserts that time is originated and created, and there is no time before it. This is the central thesis.
Notice the stark contrast with the philosophers who assume time is eternal.
2
Analyze his reinterpretation of divine priority
Examine how Ghazali explains 'God was and no world' and 'God was and the world existed' as merely indicating the existence of one essence or two, not a temporal before and after.
Priority is reduced to existence alone, not a temporal sequence.
3
Recognize the fallacy of imagination
Ghazali acknowledges that the imagination posits a third thing (time) between God and the world, but he dismisses this as a fallacy of the imagination (awham).
The imagination is not a reliable source of metaphysical truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاعتراض : هو أن يقال : الزمان حادث ومخلوق، وليس قبله زمان أصلا، ومعنى قولنا : إن الله متقدم على العالم والزمان ، أنه سبحانه كان ولا عالم ، ثم كان ومعه عالم ، ومفهوم قولنا : كان ولا عالم ، وجود الذات فقط ؛ ومفهوم قولنا : كان ومعه عالم ، وجود الذاتين فقط ، فنعنى بالتقدم انفراده بالوجود فقط ؛ والعالم كشخص واحد ، ولو قلنا : كان الله ولا عيسى مثلا ، ثم كان وعيسى معه ، لم يتضمن اللفظ إلا وجود ذات ، وعدم ذات ، ثم وجود ذاتين ، وليس من ضرورة ذلك تقدير شيء ثالث ، وإن كان الوهم لا يسكت عن تقدير شيء ثالث وهو الزمان ، فلا التفات إلى أغاليط الأوهام .
The objection: it is to say: time is originated and created, and there is no time before it at all. The meaning of our statement: 'God is prior to the world and time' is that He, exalted, was and there was no world, then He was and with Him was the world. The concept of our statement 'He was and there was no world' is only the existence of the essence. And the concept of our statement 'He was and with Hime was the world' is only the existence of the two essences. So by priority we mean only His being alone in existence. And the world is like a single person. If we said: 'God was and there was no Jesus, for example, then He was and Jesus was with Him', the expression does not imply anything except the existence of one essence and the non-existence of another essence, then the existence of two essences. And it is not necessary for that to posit a third thing. Even if the imagination does not cease from positing a third thing which is time, no attention is paid to the fallacies of imaginations.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is Ghazali's direct objection to the philosophers' second proof. He begins by asserting that time is originated and created (hadith wa makhluq), and there is no time before it at all. He then reinterprets the meaning of God's priority over the world and time: when we say 'God was and no world existed', the only meaning is the existence of God and the non-existence of the world; when we say 'God was and the world existed', it means the coexistence of two essences. Priority simply means God's existence alone first, then the existence of both. There is no need to posit a third entity like time. Ghazali compares it to saying 'God was and there was no Jesus'—the statement only conveys existence and non-existence, not a temporal interval. The imagination may conjure a 'before' as time, but that is a fallacy of the imagination (awham) and should be disregarded.

تقدم

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that saying 'God was' implies a past time, and that God's priority over the world means there was a temporal 'before' in which the world did not exist yet time did.
Correction: Ghazali explains that such a statement only means the existence of God's essence alone, with no third entity like time involved. The notion of a temporal interval is a product of the imagination, not a real entity.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali's objection, what does the phrase 'God was and no world' actually mean?
A) That time existed before the world.
B) That God's essence existed alone and the world did not exist.
C) That God is prior to time itself.
D) That there was a temporal interval before the world.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali argues that time is created and God's priority is purely existential, not temporal; the imagination's positing of a time before creation is a fallacy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about God's actions in your life—blessings, trials, delays—do you subconsciously measure them by a clock? How often do you complain about God's timing without realizing that time itself is His creation, subject to His will? Today, intentionally replace the phrase 'God's timing' with 'God's existential priority' and see how it changes your trust in His decree.
?
Ghazali says that our imagination forces us to think of a time before creation, even though none exists. Where in your own life do you imagine 'gaps' or 'waiting periods' that are actually non-existent? Are you anxious about a future that you imagine as an empty time slot? Confess that anxiety and commit to seeing every moment as a direct, seamless act of God's existence and will.

Ghazali's Response to the Linguistic Objection on 'Kana'
Objection and response on the implication of 'kana'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's argument that the past tense in 'kana' does not indicate a real temporal entity before creation, but rather a necessary relation relative to our perspective.

Core Idea
The past tense is a relation, not a reality.

The philosopher's objection based on language seems compelling: we say 'God was and no world', and 'was' implies a past that preceded creation. But Ghazali turns this around, arguing that the past tense is merely a relational concept rooted in our limited imagination. In this lesson, we'll follow his reasoning and see how he dismantles the notion of a pre-creation time.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Carefully read the entire passage, noting the objector's claim about a third concept and Ghazali's refutation. Let the original argument and counter-argument sink in.
2
Identify the objector's reasoning
The objector says 'kana' and 'yakun' differ in a third meaning beyond existence and non-existence: the past. How does he argue that this implies a real time?
He says 'kana' is only for the past, so before the world there must be time that passed.
3
Understand Ghazali's counter: relation (nisba)
Ghazali says the third factor is a 'necessary relation relative to us'. His example: the same future event can be described with 'kana' later, showing the past tense is relative.
This directly refutes the idea that 'kana' points to an absolute past.
4
Analyze the analogy with spatial imagination
Ghazali compares our inability to conceive a beginning without a 'before' to the imagination's inability to conceive finitude without an 'above'. This shows the source of the error is psychological, not metaphysical.
Just as we imagine a space beyond the world, we imagine a time before it.
5
Connect to the broader theme
Reflect on how this argument defends the Islamic doctrine of creation ex nihilo by showing that language and imagination do not necessitate a temporal prior.
This is a key move in Ghazali's critique of the philosophers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : لقولنا كان الله ولا عالم ، مفهوم ثالث سوى وجود الذات وعدم العالم ، بدليل أنا لو قدرنا عدم العالم في المستقبل ، كان وجود ذات وعدم حاصلا ، ولم يصح أن نقول : كان الله ولا عالم ، بل الصحيح أن نقول : يكون الله ولا عالم ، ونقول للماضي : كان الله ولا عالم ، فبين قولنا : ( كان ) و « يكون » فرق ، إذ ليس ينوب أحدهما مناب الآخر ، فلنبحث عما يرجع إليه الفرق ، ولا شك فى أنهما لا يفترقان فى وجود الذات ولا في عدم العالم ، بل في معنى ثالث ، فإنا إذا قلنا لعدم العالم فى المستقبل : كان الله تعالى ولا عالم ، قيل لنا : هذا خطأ ، فإنَّ « كان » إنما يقال على ما مضى . فدل أن تحت لفظ كان » مفهوماً ثالثاً ، وهو الماضى ، والماضى بذاته هو الزمان ، والماضى بغيره هو الحركة ، فإنها تمضى ببعض الزمان، فبالضرورة يلزم أن يكون قبل العالم زمان قد انقضى حتى انتهى إلى وجود العالم . قلنا : المفهوم الأصلى من اللفظين وجود ذات وعدم ، والأمر الثالث الذي به افتراق اللفظين ، نسبة لازمة بالقياس إلينا ، بدليل أنا لو قدرنا عدم العالم في المستقبل ، ثم قدرنا له بعد ذلك وجوداً ثانياً ، لكنا عند ذلك نقول : كان الله ولا عالم ، ويصح قولنا ، سواء أردنا به العدم الأول ، أو العدم الثاني الذي هو بعد الوجود ، وآية أن هذه نسبة، أن المستقبل بعينه يحوز أن يصير ماضياً فيعبر عنه بلفظ الماضى ، وهذا كله لعجز الوهم عن فهم وجود مبتدأ إلامع تقدير «قبل» له ، وذلك « القبل » الذي لا ينفك الوهم عنه ، نظن أنه شيء محقق موجود هو الزمان ، وهو كعجز الوهم عن أن يقدر تناهى الأجسام فيما يلى الرأس إلا على سطح له فوق ، فيتوهم أن وراء العالم مكاناً ، إما ملاء وإما خلاء ، وإذا قيل : ليس فوق سطح العالم فوق ، ولا بعد أبعد منه ، كاع الوهم عن
For if it is said: our statement 'God was and no world' has a third concept beyond the existence of the essence and the non-existence of the world. The evidence is that if we suppose the non-existence of the world in the future, then the existence of an essence and non-existence occur, but it would not be correct to say: 'God was and no world'; rather, it would be correct to say: 'God will be and no world'. And for the past we say: 'God was and no world'. So between our word 'was' (kana) and 'will be' (yakun) there is a difference, since one does not take the place of the other. Let us then investigate what the difference refers to. There is no doubt that they do not differ in the existence of the essence nor in the non-existence of the world, but in a third meaning. For if we say to the non-existence of the world in the future: 'God was and no world', it would be said to us: this is a mistake, for 'kana' is only said of what has passed. So it indicates that under the word 'kana' there is a third concept, which is the past. The past in itself is time, and the past by virtue of something else is motion, for it passes with some time. Necessarily then, before the world there must be a time that has elapsed until it reached the existence of the world. We say: the original concept from the two expressions is the existence of an essence and non-existence. The third matter by which the two expressions differ is a necessary relation relative to us. The proof is that if we suppose the non-existence of the world in the future, then we suppose for it a second existence afterwards, we would at that time say: 'God was and no world', and our saying would be correct, whether we mean by it the first non-existence or the second non-existence which is after existence. And the sign that this is a relation is that the very future can become past and be expressed by the past tense. All this is due to the imagination's inability to understand a beginning without positing a 'before' for it. And that 'before' from which the imagination never separates, we think it is something real existing which is time. It is like the imagination's inability to conceive of the finitude of bodies towards the head except on a surface above it, so it imagines that beyond the world there is a place, either filled or empty. And when it is said: there is no surface above the surface of the world, nor any distance beyond it, the imagination recoils from
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage contains a further objection (fain qila) and Ghazali's response (qulna). The objector argues that the difference between 'kana' (was) and 'yakun' (will be) proves there is a third concept beyond existence and non-existence: the past. Since 'kana' is used for past events, implying time has elapsed, it follows that before the world there must be a time that has passed. Ghazali responds by explaining that the third element is not a real entity but a necessary relation relative to us (nisba lazima bil-qiyas ilayna). The distinction between past and future tenses is merely a relation to our standpoint, not an independent reality. He gives an example: if we suppose future non-existence and then a second existence, we would correctly use 'kana' for the first non-existence (even though it was future when first considered). This shows that the same future event can become past, indicating that 'pastness' is a relation. The root cause is the imagination's inability to conceive a beginning without a preceding 'before', which leads it to posit time as a real entity. Ghazali compares this to the imagination's inability to conceive of the finitude of bodies without imagining something beyond—like a surface or void. Thus, the notion of a past time before creation is a fallacy of the imagination.

Key Terms

يكون
الماضى
نسبة
الوهم
القبل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The word 'kana' (was) in 'God was and no world' proves there was a real time before the world existed.
Correction: Ghazali shows that the past tense is a relational concept dependent on our perspective; the same event can be described with 'kana' or 'yakun' from different temporal standpoints, so it does not imply an absolute past.

Checkpoint
How does Ghazali explain the difference between saying 'kana' and 'yakun'?
A) It indicates a real third entity called time.
B) It is a necessary relation relative to us.
C) It proves the eternity of motion.
D) It is a purely grammatical form without meaning.

Key Takeaway
The past tense 'kana' indicates a relation, not a pre-creation time; the illusion of a temporal 'before' arises from the imagination's limitation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

This week, identify one area where you tend to project human temporal categories onto God and actively remind yourself that His attributes are beyond such limitations.
?
This lesson shows that the imagination recoils from conceiving a beginning without a 'before'. In your own life, where do you find yourself needing to imagine a 'before' in order to make sense of God's decrees? How can you trust that God's will is not bound by your mental frameworks? Write down one specific situation where you will consciously submit to God's absolute freedom from such illusions.
?
The objector assumed that the past tense implies a real time. What assumptions about God do you hold that are actually only in your own mind? What would it mean to strip those away? Choose one assumption you have about God's relationship to time or causation, and this week, whenever it arises, replace it with the recognition that God's actions are not constrained by your imagination's demands.

The Philosophers' Second Argument for Pre-Eternal Time
Ghazali presents the philosophers' second argument for the eternity of time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the structure of the philosophers' second argument for the eternity of time and how it uses the notion of measurable possibility to conclude that time must exist before the world.

Core Idea
Possibility of earlier creation implies a pre-existing measurable duration – time.

The philosophers present a sophisticated argument to prove that time is eternal. They begin with a simple observation: God could have created the world earlier by any amount. This leads them to posit a measurable interval before creation. They then refine the argument to avoid reliance on terms like 'years', using hypothetical worlds with different numbers of rotations. The argument concludes that the only reality that fits this measurable possibility is time itself, thus time must exist before the world.

Guided Path
1
Read the initial claim
Read the opening lines where the philosophers assert that God was able to create the world earlier by various amounts. Notice that they claim this implies something extended before the world.
This is the foundational premise.
2
Follow the reformulation
See how they avoid using 'years' by switching to hypothetical worlds with different numbers of rotations. This strengthens the argument by removing dependence on existing celestial motion.
3
Identify the dilemma
Notice the two possibilities they explore: either a second and third world could both reach now with equal speeds but different rotations (impossible), or they cannot, implying a measurable precedence. Understand why each leads to a conclusion that supports pre-existing time.
This is the critical turn in the argument.
4
Understand the deduction to time
Follow the reasoning that the measurable possibility (إمكان مقدر) cannot be an attribute of God or of non-existence; it must be an attribute of motion, and the measure of motion is time. Conclude that time exists before the world.
This is the final step.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider the overall proof: assuming Islamic premises (God's power to create earlier), the philosophers argue that time must be eternal. Reflect on how Ghazali sets this up for critique later.
This argument is one of the key proofs Ghazali refutes in the Tahafut.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صيغة ثانية لهم فى إلزام قدم الزمان قالوا : لا شك في أن الله عندكم كان قادراً على أن يخلق العالم قبل خلقه بقدر سنة ، ومائة سنة ، وألف سنة ، وما لا نهاية له ، وأن هذه التقديرات متفاوتة فى المقدار والكمية ، فلابد من إثبات شيء قبل وجود العالم ممتد مقدر بعضه أمد وأطول من البعض وجوده . فإن قلتم : لا يمكن إطلاق لفظ السنين إلا بعد حدوث الفلك ودورانه ، فلنترك لفظ السنين ولنورد صيغة أخرى فنقول : إذا قدرنا أن العالم من أول قد دار فلكه إلى الآن ألف دورة مثلا ، فهل كان الله سبحانه قادراً على أن يخلق قبله عالماً ثانياً مثله بحيث ينتهى إلى زماننا هذا بألف ومائة دورة ؟ فإن قلتم : لا ، فكأنه انقلب القديم من العجز إلى القدرة ، أو العالم من الإمكان إلى الاستحالة ، و إن قلتم : نعم ، ولابد منه ، فهل كان يقدر على أن يخلق عالماً ثالثاً بحيث ينتهى إلى زماننا بألف ومائتى دورة ؟ ، ولابد من نعم ، فنقول : هذا العالم الذى سميناه بحسب ترتيبنا فى التقدير ثالثاً - وإن كان هو الأسبق – فهل أمكن خلقه العالم الذى سميناه ثانياً وكان ينتهى إلينا بألفى ومائتى دورة ، والآخر بألف ومائة دورة (١) (يعنى بالآخر العالم الذي سماه « ثانيا ») ، وهما متساويان فى مسافة الحركة وسرعتها ؟ فإن قلتم : نعم ، فهو محال ، إذ يستحيل أن يتساوى حركتان في السرعة والبطء ثم تنتهيان إلى وقت واحد ، والأعداد متفاوتة ، وإن قلتم : إن العالم الثالث الذى ينتهي إلينا بألف ومائتى دورة ، لا يمكن أن يخلق مع العالم الثاني الذي ينتهي إلينا بألف ومائة دورة ، بل لابد أن يخلقه قبله بمقدار يساوى المقدار الذي تقدم به العالم الثانى على العالم الأول وسميناه الأول، لأنه أقرب إلى وهمنا، إذا ارتقنا من وقتنا إليه فى التقدير ، فيكون قدر إمكان هو ضعف إمكان آخر (١) (يعنى أن ما يسبق به العالم الثالث العالم الأول هو ضعف ما يسبق به العالم الثانى العالم الأول؛ ويمكن فرض عالم رابع يكون سبقه للعالم الأول ضعف ما يسبق به العالم الثالث العالم الأول) ، ولابد من إمكان آخر هو ضعف الكل . فهذا الإمكان المقدر بالكمية ، الذى بعضه أطول من بعض بمقدار معلوم، لا حقيقة له إلا الزمان ، فليست هذه الكميات المقدرة صفة ذات البارى تعالى عن التقدير ، ولا صفة عدم العالم ، إذ العدم ليس شيئاً حتى يقدر بمقادير مختلفة ، والكمية صفة فتستدعى ذا كمية ، وليس ذلك إلا الحركة ، والكمية إلا الزمان الذي هو قدر الحركة (٢) (أى وليست الكمية إلا الزمان) ، فإذن قبل العالم عندكم شيء ذو كمية متفاوتة ، وهو الزمان ، فقبل العالم عندكم زمان
A second formulation for them in necessitating the eternity of time. They said: There is no doubt that God, according to you, was able to create the world before its creation by a year, a hundred years, a thousand years, and what has no end, and that these estimates differ in measure and quantity; so it is necessary to establish something before the existence of the world, extended, measured, some parts longer and more extended than others, [its] existence. If you say: The term 'years' cannot be used except after the occurrence of the sphere and its rotation, so let us leave the term 'years' and present another formulation, and say: If we suppose that the world from the beginning has rotated its sphere up to now a thousand rotations, for example, was God, exalted, able to create before it a second world similar to it such that it would reach our time with a thousand and one hundred rotations? If you say: No, then it would be as if the Eternal turned from inability to ability, or the world from possibility to impossibility. And if you say: Yes, necessarily, then was He able to create a third world such that it would reach our time with a thousand and two hundred rotations? And necessarily, yes. Then we say: This world that we have named, according to our order in estimation, third—although it is the prior—was it possible to create the world we named second, which would reach us with a thousand and two hundred rotations, and the other with a thousand and one hundred rotations, while they are equal in the distance of motion and its speed? If you say: Yes, that is impossible, for it is impossible for two motions to be equal in speed and slowness and then end at one time while the numbers are different. And if you say: The third world that reaches us with a thousand and two hundred rotations cannot be created with the second world that reaches us with a thousand and one hundred rotations, but rather it must be created before it by an amount equal to the amount by which the second world preceded the first world, and we called it 'first' because it is nearer to our estimation when we ascend from our time to it in estimation, then the measure of possibility becomes double (1) another possibility, and there must be another possibility that is double of all. So this possibility measured by quantity, some parts of which are longer than others by a known amount, has no reality except time. So these measured quantities are not an attribute of the essence of the Creator—exalted above estimation—nor an attribute of the non-existence of the world, for non-existence is not a thing such that it can be measured by different measures. And quantity is an attribute, so it requires something possessing quantity, and that is only motion, and quantity is only time, which is the measure of motion. So therefore, before the world, according to you, there is something possessing varying quantity, and it is time. So before the world, according to you, there is time.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a proof: the philosophers present their second argument for the eternity of time. They begin by noting that God was able to create the world earlier by various amounts (year, centuries, etc.). This implies that there must be something extended and measurable before the world. Then they anticipate an objection: one might say that 'years' only apply after the sphere's rotation. So they reformulate the argument using hypothetical worlds with different numbers of rotations (e.g., the actual world with 1000 rotations, a second world with 1100 rotations reaching the present, etc.). They show contradictions: if a second and third world could both reach now with equal motion speeds but different rotations, it is impossible; or if the third must precede the second by a certain amount, then that amount is a measurable possibility. This measurable possibility, some parts longer than others, can only be time. It cannot be an attribute of God or of the non-existence of the world (since non-existence is not a thing). It must be an attribute of motion, and the measure of motion is time. Thus, time must exist before the world. The proof concludes: before the world there is time.

Key Terms
قدم الزمان
إمكان
كمية
دورة
حركة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument proves that time is an eternal, self-subsistent entity.
Correction: The argument only shows that according to the philosophers' assumptions (God's power to create earlier), a measurable duration must exist before the world, which they identify as time. It does not prove time is eternal in itself; rather it posits time as the measure of motion.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers' second argument, why must something measurable exist before the world?
A) Because God's power requires it.
B) Because the world's non-existence has quantity.
C) Because the possibility of creating the world earlier implies a measurable duration.
D) Because time is an attribute of God.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers attempt to prove the eternity of time by arguing that the possibility of earlier creation necessitates a measurable duration which can only be time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This argument suggests that if God could have created the world earlier, then time must have existed before creation. Do you truly believe that time is a created entity subject to God's will, or do you unconsciously think of time as an independent container? How does your answer shape your worship and reliance on God's eternal nature? Will you commit to reflecting on whether you place anything—even time—alongside God in your mind?
?
The philosophers argue that measurable possibility cannot be an attribute of God's essence. Have you ever thought of God's power in quantitative terms—like 'how much' power God has? This lesson exposes the danger of such thinking. What concrete step will you take to purify your understanding of God's attributes from human measurements?
?
If time exists before the world, then God's decision to create 'when' He did becomes bound by a temporal framework. Does that challenge your sense of God's absolute freedom? When you pray, do you imagine God 'waiting' for your prayer? Examine your hidden assumptions today and ask yourself: Am I limiting God by my understanding of time?
